--- ASSISTANT [2026-04-30 07:00:46] ---
Morning! Yes, this is all very doable. The repo already has a Blazor Server (.NET 10) skeleton, which is a great fit — same project can host the UI, the REST API, and serve as the backend for the console app. Before I draft anything I want to lock down a handful of decisions, since each has real downstream impact.

## Stack I'd propose

- **Web/API**: existing Blazor Server + Minimal API endpoints under `/api/*` (one project, one deploy).
- **DB**: SQLite via EF Core for v1 (zero-config, file-on-disk, easy backups). Trivial swap to Postgres later.
- **Auth**: Twitch OAuth — the streamer logs in with Twitch and we authorize based on his Twitch user ID matching a configured allowlist (just his ID). Cleaner than a password, and it doubles as identity for any future per-user features.
- **Video storage**: just URLs in the DB. The host (local disk + reverse proxy, S3/R2/B2, etc.) is your choice — the app stays storage-agnostic.
- **Console downloader**: a separate .NET console project in the same solution that wraps `yt-dlp` (or `TwitchDownloaderCLI`), polls Twitch's Helix API for new VODs, downloads them, uploads to your storage, and POSTs metadata to the API with a service token.

## Open questions before I plan in detail

1. **Branding** — I've got the 28 emojis but no colour palette. Want me to fetch `twitch.tv/longlivequebec` to pull his accent colour and panel art, or do you have a palette in mind? "Cave" suggests a dark, earthy theme (deep browns, warm amber accents, stone greys) with dark mode as default.
2. **Reactions** — per-viewer (need viewer login) or anonymous with one-per-IP-per-emoji? I'd lean anonymous + IP rate limiting for v1.
3. **Downloader scope** — auto-download **VODs after the stream ends** (simple, uses Helix `/videos`)? Or live-record concurrently (more complex, needs streamlink + ffmpeg)? I'd start with VODs.
4. **Game icons** — pulled automatically from Twitch's `/games` endpoint when you create a category, or manual upload? Auto is much nicer.
5. **Hosting target** — local/home server, a VPS, Azure? Affects how we wire HTTPS and storage.

## Rough plan (once decisions are locked)

**Phase 1 — Foundation**
- EF Core + SQLite, migrations, models: `Stream`, `Game`, `Emoji`, `Reaction`, `AdminUser`.
- Theme system: CSS variables, light/dark toggle persisted to `localStorage`, cave-themed palette.
- Layout shell: top bar, left sidebar (Home / Streams / Games), Twitch link, login button.
- Static assets: emojis copied into `wwwroot/emojis/`, served as `/emojis/quebX.png`.

**Phase 2 — Public site**
- Home: hero with Twitch link, 6 most-recent stream cards.
- Streams page: list + filters (game dropdown, date range, search).
- Games page: grid of game cards with icons → filtered streams.
- Stream viewer: HTML5 `<video>` against the stored URL, emoji reaction bar, reaction counts, related streams.

**Phase 3 — Auth + Admin**
- Twitch OAuth flow, role check against configured streamer ID.
- Admin pages: create game, upload/edit stream (form takes title, URL, game, date, thumbnail, description), add emoji, dashboard (total streams, total reactions, top emojis, views per stream, top games).

**Phase 4 — API**
- REST endpoints: `GET /api/streams`, `GET /api/streams/{id}`, `GET /api/games`, `GET /api/emojis`, `POST /api/reactions`, plus admin-protected `POST /api/streams`, `POST /api/games`, `POST /api/emojis`. Bearer-token auth for the console app.

**Phase 5 — Console downloader (optional)**
- Separate project: `QuebecsCave.Downloader`. Twitch Helix client, `yt-dlp` subprocess, configurable storage uploader (S3/local/SFTP), state file so it doesn't re-download. Runs as a scheduled task or `--watch` loop.

If you can answer the 5 questions above (especially 1, 3, and 5), I'll turn this into a concrete implementation plan and we can start cutting code.

# Quebec's Cave — Implementation Plan (Draft v2)

## 1. Stack

| Layer | Choice |
|---|---|
| Web + API | Blazor Server + Minimal API (single ASP.NET Core app, .NET 10) |
| Database | **MS SQL Server** via EF Core (LocalDB for dev, full SQL Server for prod) |
| Auth | Twitch OAuth (any Twitch user can sign in) |
| Hosting | **IIS** on a 24/7 local box, local disk for video storage |
| Video delivery | Static files served from a configurable local folder, exposed via IIS virtual directory or app static-files middleware |
| Console downloader | Separate .NET 10 console project, wraps `yt-dlp` |

## 2. Branding & Theme

**Palette (driven by his bear mascot):**
- **Cave Dark (default)**: bg `#1a1410` (cave wall), surface `#2d2218`, accent `#d49a3a` (honey/torch), highlight `#e8c896` (firelight), text `#f4e9d8` (parchment)
- **Forest Light**: bg `#f7efe1` (cream), surface `#fff`, accent `#a06028` (warm walnut), text `#3d2818`
- Stone-grey supporting tone `#6b5d4f` for muted UI
- Theme persisted in `localStorage`, applied via CSS variables on `<html>`
- Typography: a chunky display font for headings (Fredoka / Bricolage Grotesque), readable sans for body
- Decorative touches: subtle stone-texture backgrounds on cards, the honey accent on hovers/active states, `quebCozy` / `quebDig` etc. used as section flair

## 3. Roles & Permissions

| Role | How identified | Can do |
|---|---|---|
| **Anonymous** | not logged in | Browse home, streams, games, watch videos. No reactions. |
| **Viewer** | logged in via Twitch | Everything above + react to videos (one of each emoji per video per user) |
| **Mod** | Twitch user is in the broadcaster's moderator list | Viewer permissions + access to `/admin/reports` |
| **Streamer** | Twitch user ID matches configured `StreamerTwitchUserId` | Full admin (manage games, streams, emojis, mods cache, plus reports) |

**Mod detection** uses Twitch Helix `GET /moderation/moderators` with the streamer's stored OAuth token (scope `moderation:read`). We refresh the mod list on a timer (e.g. every 15 min) and cache it in DB. Side effect: the streamer must log in at least once so we have his refresh token; if the token ever expires unrecoverably, mods lose access until he re-auths. I'll surface a small banner on the admin dashboard if his token is stale.

## 4. Data Model (EF Core, SQL Server)

```
Game            (Id, Name, Slug, IconUrl, TwitchGameId?, IsCustomIcon, CreatedAt)
Stream          (Id, Title, Description, GameId, StreamedAt, DurationSeconds,
                 VideoUrl, ThumbnailUrl, TwitchVodId?, ViewCount, CreatedAt)
Emoji           (Id, Code, Name, ImageUrl, IsActive, SortOrder)
User            (Id, TwitchUserId, TwitchLogin, DisplayName, AvatarUrl,
                 Role [Viewer|Mod|Streamer], LastSeenAt, CreatedAt)
Reaction        (Id, StreamId, UserId, EmojiId, CreatedAt)   -- unique(StreamId, UserId, EmojiId)
StreamView      (Id, StreamId, UserId?, IpHash, ViewedAt)    -- for analytics
ModeratorCache  (TwitchUserId, TwitchLogin, RefreshedAt)
```

## 5. Pages

**Public**
- `/` — Home: hero (Twitch link, "Live now" pill if applicable later), 6 newest stream cards
- `/streams` — list, filters: game dropdown, date-range picker, search box, sort
- `/games` — grid of game cards with icons → `/games/{slug}` (prefiltered streams)
- `/streams/{id}` — viewer: HTML5 `<video>` (or Twitch embed for dummy data), reaction bar with all active emojis + counts, stream metadata
- `/login` — kicks off Twitch OAuth

**Admin (streamer only unless noted)**
- `/admin` — dashboard
- `/admin/streams` — list, create, edit, delete; upload form takes title, file (or URL), game, date, thumbnail, description
- `/admin/games` — create/edit; "Fetch from Twitch" button auto-pulls icon by game name; manual upload fallback
- `/admin/emojis` — upload/rename/toggle active
- `/admin/reports` — **also accessible to mods** — total views, total reactions, top streams, top games, reactions per emoji, growth over time, last-30-days chart

## 6. API (`/api/*`)

Public:
- `GET /api/streams` (filters: `gameId`, `from`, `to`, `q`, `take`, `skip`)
- `GET /api/streams/{id}`
- `GET /api/games`, `GET /api/games/{slug}`
- `GET /api/emojis`
- `POST /api/streams/{id}/reactions` (auth required, body: `{ emojiId }`)
- `DELETE /api/streams/{id}/reactions/{emojiId}` (auth required)
- `POST /api/streams/{id}/view` (records a view; uses user id if logged in, else hashed IP)

Admin (streamer-token or admin-cookie):
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/streams`, `/api/games`, `/api/emojis`
- `POST /api/admin/upload-video` (multipart, saves to local storage, returns URL)
- `POST /api/admin/sync-mods` (forces a Helix refresh)

Service token (for the console downloader): a long-lived API key in `appsettings`, `X-Api-Key` header, restricted to ingest endpoints.

## 7. Dummy Data

Seeded on first run if `Streams` is empty:
- ~10 streams pointing at real **Twitch VOD URLs** for `longlivequebec` (so the viewer page renders with a Twitch embed when `TwitchVodId` is set, falling back to native `<video>` when only `VideoUrl` is set). I'll fetch a handful of his real VOD IDs via Helix during seeding, or hard-code a few I find.
- 4–5 sample games (e.g. Minecraft, Stardew Valley, whatever he plays — auto-fetch icons via Helix `/games?name=`).
- All 28 emojis seeded from `wwwroot/emojis/` automatically on startup.
- A few sample reactions/views so analytics charts aren't empty.

## 8. Console Downloader (`QuebecsCave.Downloader`)

- Reads config: API base URL, API key, storage folder, Twitch client ID/secret, broadcaster ID, poll interval.
- Loop: hit Helix `GET /videos?user_id=...&type=archive`, diff against state file (`processed_vods.json`), for each new VOD:
  1. `yt-dlp -f best -o {storage}/{vodId}.mp4 https://twitch.tv/videos/{id}`
  2. Save thumbnail (Helix gives a URL).
  3. `POST /api/streams` with title/date/duration/game/url/thumbnail.
- Modes: `--once` (cron-friendly) or `--watch` (in-process loop). Logs to console + rolling file.
- Tries to auto-resolve game from VOD metadata; creates the game if missing.

## 9. Phasing

1. **Foundation** — EF Core + SQL Server, models, migrations, theme system + light/dark toggle, layout shell, emoji static assets, dummy data seeder.
2. **Public site** — Home, Streams, Games, Stream Viewer (with Twitch-embed fallback for dummy VODs).
3. **Auth + roles** — Twitch OAuth, role resolution (streamer / mod-cache / viewer), reactions wired to logged-in users.
4. **Admin** — games / streams / emojis CRUD, dashboard, reports (mods get this page).
5. **API surface** — formalize REST endpoints, service-token auth.
6. **Console downloader** — yt-dlp integration, Helix polling, ingest into API.
7. **IIS deploy** — `web.config`, app pool, virtual directory for video storage, HTTPS cert.

## Things I need from you before I start cutting code

1. **Twitch dev app**: I'll need a Client ID + Client Secret for OAuth and Helix. You can set one up at dev.twitch.tv (redirect URI `https://localhost:xxxx/auth/twitch/callback` for dev). I can stub it with placeholders until you have it.
2. **Streamer's Twitch user ID** — I can resolve this from the login `longlivequebec` once we have a client ID, or you can grab it now.
3. **SQL Server**: are you OK with `(localdb)\MSSQLLocalDB` for dev and a real SQL Server instance for prod, or do you want me to target a specific instance from the start?
4. **Storage folder convention** — something like `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\{year}\{vodId}.mp4`?

Give me thumbs up (or redirects) on any of the above and I'll start with Phase 1.

# Quebec's Cave — Implementation Plan (Draft v3)

## Replies to your points

**1) Videos** — Got it. Stored as fully-qualified URLs (e.g. `https://vod.your-domain/Minecraft/2026/12345.mp4`), our app never serves the bytes, only the URL.

**Why I pushed EF Core (and why I'm dropping it):** reflex, honestly — it's the modern .NET default I reach for first. Your reasons for `Microsoft.Data.SqlClient` are sound: no ORM magic, direct query control, fewer abstractions in the stack, and it tests just as cleanly behind a repository interface. (Quick note: `System.Data.SqlClient` is the older, frozen package; `Microsoft.Data.SqlClient` is the maintained successor — that's the one we'll use.) Migrations will be handled by **DbUp** (small library that runs versioned `.sql` scripts in order from an embedded folder) so we don't lose versioning.

**Async everywhere** — yes, all DB calls (`ExecuteReaderAsync`, `OpenAsync`), all HTTP, all `File.*Async`, all Twitch API calls. Lint rule `CA2007`/`VSTHRD200` enforced via `.editorconfig`.

**Full abstraction & unit tests** — solution becomes layered with interfaces between layers. Test projects per src project, xUnit + NSubstitute + FluentAssertions. See structure below.

**2) Theme persistence** — On load: if logged in, GET `/api/users/me/preferences`; if that returns null/anonymous, fall back to `localStorage`; default Cave Dark. On change: write to both API (if logged in) and `localStorage`.

**3) Reactions** — Made it one reaction per user per stream, changeable and removable:
- `PUT /api/streams/{id}/reaction { emojiId }` — upsert (create or change)
- `DELETE /api/streams/{id}/reaction` — remove
- DB constraint: unique `(StreamId, UserId)`
- Tell me if you actually want **multiple** simultaneous reactions per user (Discord-style) — it's a one-line constraint change.

**4) ERD style** — I pulled the Hunter Industries ERD; I'll mirror its conventions: singular PascalCase table names, PK/FK columns on the left, dedicated lookup/reference tables, an `AuditHistory` and `LoginAttempt` table, soft deletes via a `Deletion` table. ERD lives at `docs/Database ERD.drawio` so it opens in draw.io / VS Code's Drawio Integration extension.

**5) Live-now pill** — Added. Polls Helix `GET /streams?user_id={id}` every 60s on the server, broadcasts state to Blazor via a singleton service. Pill shows on home + sidebar with a glowing honey accent when live, links straight to Twitch.

**9) IIS deploy phase** — Removed.

## Things I needed back

**1) Twitch dev app redirect URIs** (use these):
- `https://localhost:7110/auth/twitch/callback` (dev)
- `https://localhost:7110/signin-twitch` (alt for ASP.NET OAuth handler — cheap to register both)
- Plus your eventual production URL when known.
- Scopes required: `user:read:email`, `moderation:read` (for mod list), `user:read:broadcast` (for VOD list — the streamer signs in once with this so the downloader has a refresh token).

**3) SQL Server** — that path is the default instance of SQL Server 2022. Connection string:
```
Server=localhost;Database=QuebecsCave;Trusted_Connection=True;TrustServerCertificate=True;
```
I'll create the DB on first run via DbUp. Tests run against `QuebecsCave_Test` on the same instance, dropped/recreated per test class.

**4) Storage path** — `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\{game-slug}\{year}\{vodId}.mp4` — game first, year inside. Slugged so spaces/special chars are safe in URLs. Thumbnails live alongside as `{vodId}.jpg`.

---

## Solution structure

```
Quebec's Cave.slnx
├── src/
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core         class lib — domain models, interfaces, enums, no I/O deps
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Data         class lib — Microsoft.Data.SqlClient repos, DbUp scripts
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services     class lib — business logic, Twitch client, file storage
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web          existing project — Blazor pages + Minimal API
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader   console — Twitch VOD watcher (yt-dlp wrapper)
├── tests/
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core.Tests          xUnit, pure unit
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Data.Tests          xUnit, integration vs LocalDB/test DB
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services.Tests      xUnit + NSubstitute mocks
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web.Tests           xUnit + bUnit (component) + WebApplicationFactory (API)
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader.Tests    xUnit + NSubstitute
└── docs/
    └── Database ERD.drawio
```

Dependency flow: `Web`/`Downloader` → `Services` → `Data` → `Core`. `Core` has zero dependencies on others. Each layer interfaces with the next via interfaces declared in `Core` (so `Services` depends on `IStreamRepository` from `Core`, implemented in `Data`).

## Database (ERD-style summary)

Singular PascalCase, PK/FK rows. Full ERD will be in `docs/Database ERD.drawio` — this is the schema it'll show:

| Table | Key cols | Notes |
|---|---|---|
| **User** | `UserId PK`, `TwitchUserId` (unique), `TwitchLogin`, `DisplayName`, `AvatarUrl`, `RoleId FK`, `ThemePreference` (enum), `CreatedUtc`, `LastSeenUtc` | |
| **Role** | `RoleId PK`, `Name` | Seed: Streamer, Moderator, Viewer |
| **Game** | `GameId PK`, `Name`, `Slug` (unique), `IconUrl`, `TwitchGameId?`, `IsCustomIcon`, `CreatedUtc` | |
| **Stream** | `StreamId PK`, `Title`, `Description`, `GameId FK`, `StreamedUtc`, `DurationSeconds`, `VideoUrl`, `ThumbnailUrl`, `TwitchVodId?`, `CreatedUtc` | |
| **Emoji** | `EmojiId PK`, `Code` (unique, e.g. `quebKing`), `Name`, `ImageUrl`, `IsActive`, `SortOrder` | |
| **Reaction** | `ReactionId PK`, `StreamId FK`, `UserId FK`, `EmojiId FK`, `CreatedUtc`, `UpdatedUtc` | unique(`StreamId`, `UserId`) |
| **StreamView** | `StreamViewId PK`, `StreamId FK`, `UserId? FK`, `IpHash`, `ViewedUtc` | |
| **ModeratorCache** | `ModeratorCacheId PK`, `TwitchUserId` (unique), `TwitchLogin`, `RefreshedUtc` | populated by Helix mod list job |
| **TwitchToken** | `TwitchTokenId PK`, `UserId FK`, `AccessToken` (encrypted), `RefreshToken` (encrypted), `ExpiresUtc`, `Scopes` | only the streamer's row is meaningful |
| **LoginAttempt** | `LoginAttemptId PK`, `TwitchUserId?`, `IpHash`, `SucceededUtc?`, `FailureReason?`, `AttemptedUtc` | |
| **AuditHistory** | `AuditHistoryId PK`, `UserId? FK`, `Entity`, `EntityId`, `Action` (Create/Update/Delete), `Diff` (json), `CreatedUtc` | written from Services on every admin mutation |
| **Deletion** | `DeletionId PK`, `Entity`, `EntityId`, `UserId? FK`, `DeletedUtc` | soft-delete record |

Indexes called out where relevant (Stream.StreamedUtc desc, Stream.GameId, Reaction unique, etc.).

## Phasing (revised)

1. **Solution restructure + Core/Data scaffold** — split current `QuebecsCave` into the layered projects, add test projects, wire up SQL Server connection + DbUp + first migration script, add ERD file, set up CI-friendly `dotnet test` config.
2. **Theme system + layout shell** — Cave Dark / Forest Light CSS variables, toggle, persistence (localStorage now, API later in phase 3).
3. **Public site + dummy data** — home, streams list with filters, games grid, stream viewer (Twitch embed when `TwitchVodId` set, native `<video>` otherwise), seed of ~10 streams pointing at his real Twitch VOD IDs and the 28 emojis.
4. **Twitch OAuth + roles + theme-in-API** — login flow, role resolution (streamer ID match → mod cache → viewer), `/api/users/me/preferences` for theme.
5. **Reactions** — PUT/DELETE endpoints, UI on stream viewer, live counts, change/remove behaviour, IP rate limit on the endpoint as defence-in-depth.
6. **Live-now pill** — Helix poller hosted service + signal to UI.
7. **Admin** — game / stream / emoji CRUD, moderator-list refresh, dashboard + reports (mods see reports only).
8. **Public + admin REST API surface** — formalised, OpenAPI doc generated, service-token auth for the downloader.
9. **Console downloader** — Twitch Helix poller, yt-dlp wrapper, file mover into `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\{game-slug}\{year}\{vodId}.mp4`, ingest call to API. `--once` and `--watch` modes, structured logging.
10. **Test pass** — fill any gaps so every project has meaningful unit + (where appropriate) integration coverage.

Two quick yes/no checks before I touch code:

- **One reaction per user per stream** (changeable/removable) is the right read of your requirement, correct?
- **xUnit + NSubstitute + FluentAssertions + bUnit** for the test stack — happy with that, or do you have a preference?

# Quebec's Cave — Implementation Plan (Draft v4)

## Replies to your points

**3) Reactions — Discord-style** ✓ Multiple per user per stream. Each emoji is independently toggleable.
- DB: unique `(StreamId, UserId, EmojiId)` (back to the v2 model)
- Endpoints: `POST /api/streams/{id}/reactions { emojiId }` to add, `DELETE /api/streams/{id}/reactions/{emojiId}` to remove. Idempotent — re-POSTing the same emoji is a no-op.
- UI: stream viewer shows the full emoji bar; clicking toggles your own state (lit / unlit) and increments/decrements the count.

## Things you needed

**1) Twitch scopes** — short answer: you don't register scopes in the dev console. Twitch's OAuth model passes scopes at *login time* via the `scope=` query parameter on the `/oauth2/authorize` URL. The dev console only cares about:
- **Name**
- **OAuth Redirect URLs** — add `https://localhost:7110/signin-twitch` (this is the default ASP.NET OAuth callback path; no app code needed for it). Add the eventual prod URL when you have one.
- **Category** — pick "Website Integration" or similar
- **Client Type** — **Confidential** (we have a server, so we can keep the secret)

Scopes I'll request at runtime: `user:read:email` (basic identity), `moderation:read` (so the streamer's token can fetch the mod list), `user:read:broadcast` (so the streamer's token can list his own VODs for the downloader).

For the credentials in your `Credentials.txt`: I'll wire them via .NET User Secrets in dev so they don't land in `appsettings.json` or git. Command in the Web project will be `dotnet user-secrets set "Twitch:ClientId" "..."` etc. For prod, environment variables.

**3) Tests — mock abstractions only, no DB hits** ✓ Dropping the integration-test project. Strategy:
- `QuebecsCave.Data` is exercised purely at runtime; not unit-tested.
- All meaningful logic lives in `QuebecsCave.Services` and is tested with Moq-faked `IStreamRepository`, `IUserRepository`, `ITwitchClient`, `IFileStorage` etc.
- `QuebecsCave.Web` tests use bUnit for components + `WebApplicationFactory` for endpoints, with the repo layer fully mocked.
- `QuebecsCave.Core` tests cover any domain logic (e.g. slug generation, role resolution rules, validation).
- `QuebecsCave.Downloader` tests mock the Twitch client, yt-dlp wrapper, and HTTP client.

**Test stack — MSTest + Moq** (matching your other projects)
- `Microsoft.NET.Test.Sdk` + `MSTest.TestAdapter` + `MSTest.TestFramework`
- `Moq` for mocks
- `FluentAssertions` for assertions (works with MSTest)
- `bUnit` for Blazor components (works with MSTest)
- Naming: `[TestClass]` + `[TestMethod]`, `MethodName_Scenario_ExpectedOutcome`

## Updated solution structure

```
Quebec's Cave.slnx
├── src/
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core         class lib — domain, interfaces, enums, no I/O deps
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Data         class lib — Microsoft.Data.SqlClient repos, DbUp scripts (NOT unit-tested)
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services     class lib — business logic, Twitch client, file storage
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web          existing — Blazor + Minimal API
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader   console — Twitch VOD watcher
├── tests/                       MSTest + Moq + FluentAssertions

```

## Migration clarification

Fair pushback — let me be precise about what I mean.

**EF Core migrations** generate C# code that mutates the schema. We're not doing that.

What I was calling "migrations" is just **versioned SQL scripts** — plain `.sql` files like `001_CreateUserTable.sql`, `002_AddReactionTable.sql`, `003_AddIsActiveToEmoji.sql`. The schema has to be created somehow on first run, and as features land it has to evolve — versioned scripts are how you do that without manually `ALTER`-ing the DB on each box.

You've got three reasonable options here:

1. **DbUp** (what I proposed) — a tiny library (~50KB, zero dependencies) that runs your `.sql` scripts in order on app startup and tracks which have run in a `SchemaVersions` table it manages. Doesn't conflict with `Microsoft.Data.SqlClient` in any way — DbUp just executes the SQL you write, you still write everything by hand.
2. **Hand-rolled migrator** — same idea, ~80 lines of code in `QuebecsCave.Data`: at startup, read embedded `.sql` files, check a `SchemaVersions` table, run any that haven't been run. Removes the dependency.
3. **Single bootstrap script, run manually** — one `schema.sql` you keep up to date and run yourself when deploying. Simplest, but you have to remember to run it and reason about diffs by hand.

My recommendation is **(1)** for the dev velocity, but **(2)** is genuinely fine if you'd prefer no third-party deps in the data layer. **(3)** I'd avoid — it'll bite once there's prod data you can't drop. Tell me which you want and I'll bake it in.

**Prod credentials in `appsettings.json` / `app.config`** — noted. I'll respect that. ASP.NET Core uses `appsettings.json`; `app.config` is the .NET Framework convention. The web project will read from `appsettings.json` (with a `appsettings.Production.json` overlay you place on the prod box). Just make sure that prod file is **not** committed — your `.gitignore` should cover it. The downloader console can use either pattern; I'll mirror it to `appsettings.json` for consistency.

**Redirect URL approved** ✓

# Quebec's Cave — Full Implementation Plan (v5)

## 1. Stack

| Layer | Choice |
|---|---|
| Web + API | Blazor Server + Minimal API (one ASP.NET Core app, .NET 10) |
| Database | MS SQL Server (local default instance), accessed via `Microsoft.Data.SqlClient` |
| Schema versioning | DbUp (or hand-rolled — your call) running embedded `.sql` scripts |
| Auth | Twitch OAuth (any Twitch user can sign in) |
| Console downloader | .NET 10 console wrapping `yt-dlp` |
| Test stack | MSTest + Moq + FluentAssertions + bUnit (Blazor components) + WebApplicationFactory (API) |
| Secrets in dev | .NET User Secrets |
| Secrets in prod | `appsettings.Production.json` placed on the prod box, gitignored |
| Hosting | IIS on a 24/7 local box (you'll handle deploy) |
| Video delivery | Separate IIS site serves files from `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\...` at e.g. `https://vod.your-domain/...`. App stores URLs only. |

**Cross-cutting rules:**
- Async on every I/O method (DB, HTTP, file). Public methods accept `CancellationToken` where they can.
- Repository interfaces in `Core`, implementations in `Data`. Services depend on interfaces.
- All admin mutations write to `AuditHistory`. Soft delete via `Deletion` table.

## 2. Solution structure

```
Quebec's Cave.slnx
├── src/
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core         class lib — POCOs, interfaces, enums, validation. No I/O deps.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Data         class lib — Microsoft.Data.SqlClient repos, embedded SQL scripts, DbUp.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services     class lib — business logic, Twitch Helix client, file storage, time provider.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web          existing — Blazor pages + Minimal API endpoints.
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader   console — Twitch VOD watcher (yt-dlp wrapper).
├── tests/                       MSTest + Moq + FluentAssertions
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core.Tests
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services.Tests          (mocks IXxxRepository, ITwitchClient, IFileStorage)
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web.Tests               (+ bUnit for components, WebApplicationFactory for API)
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader.Tests
└── docs/
    └── Database ERD.drawio
```

Dependency flow: `Web` & `Downloader` → `Services` → `Data` → `Core`. `Core` depends on nothing.

## 3. Branding & theme

**Cave Dark (default)**: bg `#1a1410` · surface `#2d2218` · accent `#d49a3a` · highlight `#e8c896` · text `#f4e9d8` · muted stone `#6b5d4f`.
**Forest Light**: bg `#f7efe1` · surface `#ffffff` · accent `#a06028` · text `#3d2818`.

- Theme applied via CSS variables on `<html data-theme="dark|light">`.
- Headings: chunky display font (Fredoka or Bricolage Grotesque). Body: readable sans (Inter).
- Subtle stone-texture backgrounds on cards. Honey accent for hover/active. Mascot emojis (`quebCozy`, `quebDig`, `quebRaid` etc.) used as section flair.
- Logo placeholder at top-left links to home; sidebar holds Streams + Games + Twitch link + login/profile + theme toggle.

## 4. Roles & permissions

| Role | Resolution | Capabilities |
|---|---|---|
| Anonymous | not logged in | Browse home, streams, games, watch videos |
| Viewer | logged in via Twitch | + react to videos |
| Moderator | Twitch user is in `ModeratorCache` (refreshed via Helix `/moderation/moderators`) | + access `/admin/reports` |
| Streamer | Twitch user ID matches `Twitch:StreamerUserId` config | + full admin (games, streams, emojis, mod cache refresh, reports) |

The streamer must log in once with `moderation:read` and `user:read:broadcast` scopes so we have his refresh token; a hosted service refreshes the mod cache every 15 min. If his token ever expires unrecoverably, a banner on the admin dashboard tells him to re-auth.

## 5. Database (full schema)

ERD style mirrors the Hunter Industries reference: singular PascalCase, PK/FK rows. Full diagram lives at `docs/Database ERD.drawio`.

```
Role
  RoleId          PK   int identity
  Name            varchar(20)              -- Streamer | Moderator | Viewer

User
  UserId          PK   int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  unique
  TwitchLogin     varchar(50)
  DisplayName     nvarchar(100)
  AvatarUrl       varchar(500)
  RoleId          FK → Role.RoleId
  ThemePreference varchar(10)  null         -- 'dark' | 'light' | null
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  LastSeenUtc     datetime2

Game
  GameId          PK   int identity
  Name            nvarchar(150)
  Slug            varchar(150)  unique
  IconUrl         varchar(500)
  TwitchGameId    varchar(50)   null
  IsCustomIcon    bit
  CreatedUtc      datetime2

Stream
  StreamId        PK   int identity
  Title           nvarchar(300)
  Description     nvarchar(max) null
  GameId          FK → Game.GameId
  StreamedUtc     datetime2
  DurationSeconds int
  VideoUrl        varchar(500)
  ThumbnailUrl    varchar(500)
  TwitchVodId     varchar(50)   null
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  -- index on (StreamedUtc desc), (GameId)

Emoji
  EmojiId         PK   int identity
  Code            varchar(50)   unique     -- e.g. 'quebKing'
  Name            varchar(100)
  ImageUrl        varchar(500)
  IsActive        bit
  SortOrder       int

Reaction
  ReactionId      PK   int identity
  StreamId        FK → Stream.StreamId
  UserId          FK → User.UserId
  EmojiId         FK → Emoji.EmojiId
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  -- unique(StreamId, UserId, EmojiId)   ← Discord-style multi

StreamView
  StreamViewId    PK   int identity
  StreamId        FK → Stream.StreamId
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  IpHash          varbinary(32)              -- SHA-256
  ViewedUtc       datetime2

ModeratorCache
  ModeratorCacheId PK  int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  unique
  TwitchLogin     varchar(50)
  RefreshedUtc    datetime2

TwitchToken
  TwitchTokenId   PK   int identity
  UserId          FK → User.UserId
  AccessToken     varbinary(max)            -- DPAPI-encrypted
  RefreshToken    varbinary(max)            -- DPAPI-encrypted
  ExpiresUtc      datetime2
  Scopes          varchar(500)

LoginAttempt
  LoginAttemptId  PK   int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  null
  IpHash          varbinary(32)
  SucceededUtc    datetime2    null
  FailureReason   varchar(200) null
  AttemptedUtc    datetime2

AuditHistory
  AuditHistoryId  PK   int identity
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  Entity          varchar(50)
  EntityId        int
  Action          varchar(20)               -- Create | Update | Delete
  Diff            nvarchar(max)             -- json
  CreatedUtc      datetime2

Deletion
  DeletionId      PK   int identity
  Entity          varchar(50)
  EntityId        int
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  DeletedUtc      datetime2
```

## 6. Pages

**Public**
- `/` Home — hero with Twitch link, **live-now pill** (glows when live), 6 newest stream cards.
- `/streams` — list with filters: game dropdown, date-range picker, free-text search, sort.
- `/games` — grid of game cards with icons → `/games/{slug}` (prefiltered streams).
- `/streams/{id}` — viewer: HTML5 `<video src="…">` (or Twitch embed when `TwitchVodId` is set, for dummy data), Discord-style emoji reaction bar, related streams.
- `/login` — kicks off Twitch OAuth.

**Admin (streamer only unless flagged)**
- `/admin` dashboard.
- `/admin/streams` — list + create/edit/delete; form has title, video URL (or upload to local storage), game, date, thumbnail, description.
- `/admin/games` — create/edit; "Fetch icon from Twitch" button via Helix `/games?name=`, manual upload fallback.
- `/admin/emojis` — upload PNG, set code/name, toggle active, reorder.
- `/admin/reports` — **mods + streamer** — total views, total reactions, top streams, top games, reactions per emoji, growth over time, last-30-days chart.

## 7. API

**Public**
- `GET /api/streams?gameId=&from=&to=&q=&take=&skip=`
- `GET /api/streams/{id}`
- `GET /api/games`, `GET /api/games/{slug}`
- `GET /api/emojis`
- `GET /api/live-status` (cached Helix poll result)
- `POST /api/streams/{id}/view` (anonymous OK; uses user id if logged in else hashed IP)

**Authenticated viewer**
- `POST /api/streams/{id}/reactions { emojiId }` — add (idempotent)
- `DELETE /api/streams/{id}/reactions/{emojiId}` — remove
- `GET /api/users/me`
- `GET/PUT /api/users/me/preferences { theme }`

**Mod or Streamer**
- `GET /api/admin/reports/*`

**Streamer only**
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/streams`
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/games`
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/emojis`
- `POST /api/admin/upload-video` (multipart; saves under `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\{game-slug}\{year}\{vodId}.mp4`)
- `POST /api/admin/sync-mods`

**Service token (X-Api-Key, used by downloader)**
- `POST /api/ingest/streams` — create a stream from VOD metadata
- `GET /api/ingest/known-vod-ids` — for diff against Helix

## 8. Reactions (Discord-style)

- Multiple emojis per user per stream. Each emoji is independently toggleable.
- DB: unique `(StreamId, UserId, EmojiId)`.
- API: `POST .../reactions {emojiId}` (idempotent — re-POST is a no-op), `DELETE .../reactions/{emojiId}`.
- UI: emoji bar on the viewer page; each chip shows count + lit/unlit state for current user. Click = toggle.
- IP rate limit on POST/DELETE as defence-in-depth (e.g. 60 actions / 60s / IP).

## 9. Live-now pill

- A `LiveStatusBackgroundService` polls Helix `GET /streams?user_id=...` every 60s (configurable) using an app-credentials token.
- State exposed via singleton `ILiveStatusService` consumed by Blazor + the `/api/live-status` endpoint.
- Pill rendered in the top bar; glowing honey accent + "LIVE" label + "Currently playing X" when live, hidden otherwise. Clicks open `https://twitch.tv/longlivequebec`.

## 10. Theme persistence

- On page load (after auth check):
  - If logged in → `GET /api/users/me/preferences`. If `theme` set → apply.
  - Else → read `localStorage["theme"]`. If set → apply.
  - Else → default Cave Dark.
- On toggle:
  - Always write to `localStorage`.
  - If logged in → also `PUT /api/users/me/preferences { theme }`.
- On login → if API has no theme but `localStorage` does, push it up.

## 11. Dummy data (seeded if `Stream` is empty)

- All 28 emojis from `wwwroot/emojis/quebX.png`, populated into `Emoji` with `Code = quebX`, sensible `SortOrder`.
- 4–5 sample games, icons fetched via Helix `/games?name=` at seed time.
- ~10 sample streams pointing at real `longlivequebec` Twitch VOD IDs (so `TwitchVodId` is set and the viewer renders the Twitch embed). I'll resolve the IDs at seed time via Helix `/videos?user_id=...` once we have the Client ID/Secret loaded.
- Sample reactions + views so `/admin/reports` has something to render.

## 12. Console downloader (`QuebecsCave.Downloader`)

- Reads from `appsettings.json`: API base URL, service API key, storage root, Twitch Client ID/Secret, broadcaster user ID, poll interval seconds.
- Loop logic:
  1. Get app token (client credentials) → list VODs via `GET /helix/videos?user_id=...&type=archive`.
  2. Diff against `GET /api/ingest/known-vod-ids`.
  3. For each new VOD: `yt-dlp -f best -o "{root}/{game-slug}/{year}/{vodId}.mp4" "https://twitch.tv/videos/{vodId}"`, also save thumbnail.
  4. `POST /api/ingest/streams` with metadata.
- Modes: `--once` (cron-friendly) or `--watch` (in-process loop).
- Structured logging to console + rolling file via `Microsoft.Extensions.Logging` + Serilog.

## 13. Configuration

```jsonc
// appsettings.json (committed, no secrets)
{
  "ConnectionStrings": {
    "Default": "Server=localhost;Database=QuebecsCave;Trusted_Connection=True;TrustServerCertificate=True;"
  },
  "Twitch": {
    "ClientId": "",                    // dev: user-secrets; prod: appsettings.Production.json
    "ClientSecret": "",
    "StreamerUserId": "",              // resolved once and pasted in
    "RedirectPath": "/signin-twitch",
    "ModRefreshSeconds": 900,
    "LiveStatusPollSeconds": 60
  },
  "Storage": {
    "VideoRoot": "D:\\QuebecsCave\\videos",
    "PublicBaseUrl": "https://vod.your-domain"
  },
  "Api": {
    "ServiceKeys": []                  // for downloader; set in prod overlay
  }
}
```

`.gitignore` covers `appsettings.Production.json`, `appsettings.Development.json` (also overridden by user secrets), and the user-secrets store.

## 14. Phasing (revised, no IIS phase)

1. **Solution restructure + scaffolding** — create Core/Data/Services/Web/Downloader projects + four MSTest test projects. Wire DbUp (or hand-rolled) + first SQL script with the full schema above. Drop `docs/Database ERD.drawio`. Connection string + user-secrets bootstrap.
2. **Theme system + layout shell** — Cave Dark / Forest Light CSS vars, toggle, sidebar, top bar, mascot flair, theme persistence (localStorage path; API path lands in phase 4).
3. **Public site + dummy data** — home (no live pill yet), streams list with filters, games grid, stream viewer with Twitch embed for dummy VODs, all 28 emojis seeded.
4. **Twitch OAuth + roles + theme-in-API** — login, role resolution (streamer match → mod cache → viewer), `/api/users/me/preferences`. Mod-cache refresh background service.
5. **Reactions** — endpoints, UI bar, counts, IP rate limit.
6. **Live-now pill** — Helix poller + UI badge + endpoint.
7. **Admin pages** — games / streams / emojis CRUD, dashboard, reports (mods get reports). `AuditHistory` and `Deletion` writes.
8. **Public + admin REST API surface** — formalise contracts, OpenAPI doc via `Microsoft.AspNetCore.OpenApi`, service-key auth for ingest endpoints.
9. **Console downloader** — Twitch Helix poller, yt-dlp wrapper, file mover, ingest-API client. `--once` and `--watch` modes.
10. **Test pass** — sweep each src project for gaps; aim for meaningful coverage of all branching logic in Core + Services + Web + Downloader.

**Quick note on dev config naming**: ASP.NET Core's auto-loader expects `appsettings.{Environment}.json` — i.e. **`appsettings.Development.json`** (dot, capital D), not the hyphen form you wrote. If we use the hyphen form the framework won't pick it up automatically and we'd have to wire it manually. I'm using the dot-convention in the plan; tell me if you actually want the hyphen and I'll add an explicit `AddJsonFile("appsettings-development.json", optional: true)` call. Same for the downloader — both projects are .NET 10 so they use `appsettings.json`, not `app.config` (which is the .NET Framework world).

# Quebec's Cave — Full Implementation Plan (v6)

## 1. Stack

| Layer | Choice |
|---|---|
| Web + API | Blazor Server + Minimal API (one ASP.NET Core app, .NET 10) |
| Database | MS SQL Server (local default instance), accessed via `Microsoft.Data.SqlClient` |
| Schema versioning | DbUp running embedded `.sql` scripts on startup |
| Auth | Twitch OAuth |
| Console downloader | .NET 10 console wrapping `yt-dlp` |
| Test stack | MSTest + Moq + FluentAssertions + bUnit + WebApplicationFactory |
| Secrets — dev | `appsettings.Development.json` (gitignored) |
| Secrets — prod | `appsettings.json` placed on the prod box (gitignored real values; committed file holds blanks/defaults) |
| Hosting | IIS on a 24/7 local box (you'll handle deploy) |
| Video delivery | Separate IIS site serving `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\...` at `https://vod.your-domain/...`. App stores URLs only. |

**Cross-cutting rules:**
- Async on every I/O method (DB, HTTP, file). Public methods accept `CancellationToken` where they can.
- Repository interfaces in `Core`, implementations in `Data`. Services depend on interfaces only.
- All admin mutations write to `AuditHistory`. Soft delete via `Deletion`.

## 2. Solution structure

```
Quebec's Cave.slnx
├── src/
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core         class lib — POCOs, interfaces, enums, validation. No I/O deps.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Data         class lib — Microsoft.Data.SqlClient repos, embedded SQL scripts, DbUp.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services     class lib — business logic, Twitch Helix client, file storage, time provider.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web          existing — Blazor pages + Minimal API endpoints.
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader   console — Twitch VOD watcher (yt-dlp wrapper).
├── tests/                       MSTest + Moq + FluentAssertions
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core.Tests
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services.Tests          (mocks IXxxRepository, ITwitchClient, IFileStorage)
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web.Tests               (+ bUnit, + WebApplicationFactory)
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader.Tests
└── docs/
    └── Database ERD.drawio
```

Dependency flow: `Web` & `Downloader` → `Services` → `Data` → `Core`. `Core` depends on nothing.

## 3. Branding & theme

**Cave Dark (default)**: bg `#1a1410` · surface `#2d2218` · accent `#d49a3a` · highlight `#e8c896` · text `#f4e9d8` · muted stone `#6b5d4f`.
**Forest Light**: bg `#f7efe1` · surface `#ffffff` · accent `#a06028` · text `#3d2818`.

- Theme applied via CSS variables on `<html data-theme="dark|light">`.
- Headings: chunky display font (Fredoka or Bricolage Grotesque). Body: Inter.
- Subtle stone-texture backgrounds on cards. Honey accent for hover/active. Mascot emojis (`quebCozy`, `quebDig`, `quebRaid`, etc.) used as section flair.
- Streamer's Twitch profile image used as the header logo (linked from his Twitch CDN URL above, with a local cached fallback).
- Sidebar holds Streams + Games + Twitch link + login/profile + theme toggle.

## 4. Roles & permissions

| Role | Resolution | Capabilities |
|---|---|---|
| Anonymous | not logged in | Browse home, streams, games, watch videos |
| Viewer | logged in via Twitch | + react to videos |
| Moderator | Twitch user is in `ModeratorCache` (refreshed via Helix `/moderation/moderators`) | + access `/admin/reports` |
| Streamer | Twitch user ID = **`[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]`** | + full admin (games, streams, emojis, mod cache refresh, reports) |

The streamer must log in once with `moderation:read` and `user:read:broadcast` scopes so we hold his refresh token; a hosted service refreshes the mod cache every 15 min. If his token expires unrecoverably, a banner on the admin dashboard tells him to re-auth.

## 5. Database (full schema)

ERD style mirrors the Hunter Industries reference: singular PascalCase, PK/FK rows, dedicated `AuditHistory` / `LoginAttempt` / `Deletion` lookup-style tables. Full diagram lives at `docs/Database ERD.drawio`.

```
Role
  RoleId          PK   int identity
  Name            varchar(20)              -- Streamer | Moderator | Viewer

User
  UserId          PK   int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  unique
  TwitchLogin     varchar(50)
  DisplayName     nvarchar(100)
  AvatarUrl       varchar(500)
  RoleId          FK → Role.RoleId
  ThemePreference varchar(10)  null         -- 'dark' | 'light' | null
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  LastSeenUtc     datetime2

Game
  GameId          PK   int identity
  Name            nvarchar(150)
  Slug            varchar(150)  unique
  IconUrl         varchar(500)
  TwitchGameId    varchar(50)   null
  IsCustomIcon    bit
  CreatedUtc      datetime2

Stream
  StreamId        PK   int identity
  Title           nvarchar(300)
  Description     nvarchar(max) null
  GameId          FK → Game.GameId
  StreamedUtc     datetime2
  DurationSeconds int
  VideoUrl        varchar(500)
  ThumbnailUrl    varchar(500)
  TwitchVodId     varchar(50)   null
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  -- index on (StreamedUtc desc), (GameId)

Emoji
  EmojiId         PK   int identity
  Code            varchar(50)   unique     -- e.g. 'quebKing'
  Name            varchar(100)
  ImageUrl        varchar(500)
  IsActive        bit
  SortOrder       int

Reaction
  ReactionId      PK   int identity
  StreamId        FK → Stream.StreamId
  UserId          FK → User.UserId
  EmojiId         FK → Emoji.EmojiId
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  -- unique(StreamId, UserId, EmojiId)   ← Discord-style multi

StreamView
  StreamViewId    PK   int identity
  StreamId        FK → Stream.StreamId
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  IpHash          varbinary(32)              -- SHA-256
  ViewedUtc       datetime2

ModeratorCache
  ModeratorCacheId PK  int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  unique
  TwitchLogin     varchar(50)
  RefreshedUtc    datetime2

TwitchToken
  TwitchTokenId   PK   int identity
  UserId          FK → User.UserId
  AccessToken     varbinary(max)            -- DPAPI-encrypted
  RefreshToken    varbinary(max)            -- DPAPI-encrypted
  ExpiresUtc      datetime2
  Scopes          varchar(500)

LoginAttempt
  LoginAttemptId  PK   int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  null
  IpHash          varbinary(32)
  SucceededUtc    datetime2    null
  FailureReason   varchar(200) null
  AttemptedUtc    datetime2

AuditHistory
  AuditHistoryId  PK   int identity
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  Entity          varchar(50)
  EntityId        int
  Action          varchar(20)               -- Create | Update | Delete
  Diff            nvarchar(max)             -- json
  CreatedUtc      datetime2

Deletion
  DeletionId      PK   int identity
  Entity          varchar(50)
  EntityId        int
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  DeletedUtc      datetime2
```

## 6. Pages

**Public**
- `/` Home — hero with Twitch link, **live-now pill** (glows when live), 6 newest stream cards.
- `/streams` — list with filters: game dropdown, date-range picker, free-text search, sort.
- `/games` — grid of game cards with icons → `/games/{slug}` (prefiltered streams).
- `/streams/{id}` — viewer: HTML5 `<video>` (or Twitch embed when `TwitchVodId` is set, for dummy data), Discord-style emoji reaction bar, related streams.
- `/login` — kicks off Twitch OAuth.

**Admin (streamer only unless flagged)**
- `/admin` — dashboard.
- `/admin/streams` — list + create/edit/delete; form has title, video URL (or upload to local storage), game, date, thumbnail, description.
- `/admin/games` — create/edit; "Fetch icon from Twitch" button via Helix `/games?name=`, manual upload fallback.
- `/admin/emojis` — upload PNG, set code/name, toggle active, reorder.
- `/admin/reports` — **mods + streamer** — total views, total reactions, top streams, top games, reactions per emoji, growth over time, last-30-days chart.

## 7. API

**Public**
- `GET /api/streams?gameId=&from=&to=&q=&take=&skip=`
- `GET /api/streams/{id}`
- `GET /api/games`, `GET /api/games/{slug}`
- `GET /api/emojis`
- `GET /api/live-status` (cached Helix poll result)
- `POST /api/streams/{id}/view` (anonymous OK; uses user id if logged in else hashed IP)

**Authenticated viewer**
- `POST /api/streams/{id}/reactions { emojiId }` — add (idempotent)
- `DELETE /api/streams/{id}/reactions/{emojiId}` — remove
- `GET /api/users/me`
- `GET/PUT /api/users/me/preferences { theme }`

**Mod or Streamer**
- `GET /api/admin/reports/*`

**Streamer only**
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/streams`
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/games`
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/emojis`
- `POST /api/admin/upload-video` (multipart; saves under `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\{game-slug}\{year}\{vodId}.mp4`)
- `POST /api/admin/sync-mods`

**Service token (X-Api-Key, used by downloader)**
- `POST /api/ingest/streams`
- `GET /api/ingest/known-vod-ids`

## 8. Reactions (Discord-style)

- Multiple emojis per user per stream. Each emoji is independently toggleable.
- DB unique key: `(StreamId, UserId, EmojiId)`.
- API: `POST .../reactions {emojiId}` (idempotent), `DELETE .../reactions/{emojiId}`.
- UI: emoji bar on the viewer page; each chip shows count + lit/unlit state for current user.
- IP rate limit on POST/DELETE as defence-in-depth (e.g. 60 actions / 60s / IP).

## 9. Live-now pill

- `LiveStatusBackgroundService` polls Helix `GET /streams?user_id=[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]` every 60s using an app-credentials token.
- State exposed via singleton `ILiveStatusService` consumed by Blazor + the `/api/live-status` endpoint.
- Pill in the top bar; glowing honey accent + "LIVE" label + "Currently playing X" when live; hidden otherwise. Click → `https://twitch.tv/longlivequebec`.

## 10. Theme persistence

- On load:
  - If logged in → `GET /api/users/me/preferences`. If `theme` set, apply.
  - Else → read `localStorage["theme"]`. If set, apply.
  - Else → default Cave Dark.
- On toggle:
  - Always write `localStorage`.
  - If logged in → also `PUT /api/users/me/preferences { theme }`.
- On login → if API has no theme but `localStorage` does, push it up.

## 11. Dummy data (seeded if `Stream` is empty)

- All 28 emojis from `wwwroot/emojis/quebX.png`, populated into `Emoji` with `Code = quebX`.
- 4–5 sample games, icons fetched via Helix `/games?name=` at seed time.
- ~10 sample streams pointing at real `longlivequebec` Twitch VOD IDs (resolved via Helix `/videos?user_id=[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]&type=archive` at seed time). Viewer renders the Twitch embed for these.
- Sample reactions + views so `/admin/reports` has something to render.

## 12. Console downloader (`QuebecsCave.Downloader`)

- Reads `appsettings.json` (+ `appsettings.Development.json` overlay): API base URL, service API key, storage root, Twitch Client ID/Secret, broadcaster user ID `[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]`, poll interval seconds.
- Loop:
  1. Get app token (client credentials) → list VODs via `GET /helix/videos?user_id=[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]&type=archive`.
  2. Diff against `GET /api/ingest/known-vod-ids`.
  3. For each new VOD: `yt-dlp -f best -o "{root}/{game-slug}/{year}/{vodId}.mp4" "https://twitch.tv/videos/{vodId}"`, also save thumbnail.
  4. `POST /api/ingest/streams` with metadata.
- Modes: `--once` (cron-friendly) or `--watch` (in-process loop).
- Logging via `Microsoft.Extensions.Logging` + Serilog console + rolling file.

## 13. Configuration

```jsonc

{
  "ConnectionStrings": {
    "Default": "Server=localhost;Database=QuebecsCave;Trusted_Connection=True;TrustServerCertificate=True;"
  },
  "Twitch": {
    "ClientId": "",
    "ClientSecret": "",
    "StreamerUserId": "[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]",
    "StreamerLogin": "longlivequebec",
    "RedirectPath": "/signin-twitch",
    "ModRefreshSeconds": 900,
    "LiveStatusPollSeconds": 60
  },
  "Storage": {
    "VideoRoot": "D:\\QuebecsCave\\videos",
    "PublicBaseUrl": "https://vod.your-domain"
  },
  "Api": {
    "ServiceKeys": []
  }
}
```

```jsonc

{

    "ClientId":     "[REDACTED-CLIENT-ID]",
    "ClientSecret": "[REDACTED-CLIENT-SECRET]"
  },
```


`.gitignore` will cover `appsettings.Development.json` everywhere.

--- ASSISTANT [2026-04-30 08:06:10] ---
It's not coming from anywhere — that placeholder is a value **we generate** ourselves. It's the shared secret that lets the downloader authenticate to the Web API's ingest endpoints.

The flow:
- Web (`appsettings.Development.json`): `"Api": { "ServiceKeys": [ "<key>" ] }` — the allowlist the API accepts.
- Downloader (`appsettings.Development.json`): `"Api": { "ServiceKey": "<key>" }` — what it sends in the `X-Api-Key` header on every ingest call.
- Both files hold the same string. Web compares incoming header against its allowlist (constant-time compare); match → ingest allowed.

It exists because the ingest endpoints (`POST /api/ingest/streams`) need *some* form of auth — they're not user-facing, so Twitch OAuth doesn't apply, and they're machine-to-machine, so a static key is the simplest fit.

It just needs to be a long random string. Any of these work:

```bash
# Bash / git-bash
openssl rand -base64 32
```
```powershell
# PowerShell
[Convert]::ToBase64String([byte[]](1..32 | %{ Get-Random -Max 256 }))
```

Want me to generate one now and bake it into both config files in Phase 1? Or you can paste your own — the Web side accepts an array, so you can rotate/add keys without downtime.

--- ASSISTANT [2026-04-30 08:11:29] ---
Got it. That key goes into the dev configs, and I'll lock down **every** `/api/*` endpoint behind the `X-Api-Key` header. User-specific and admin endpoints still layer Twitch OAuth + role checks on top — so it's two-stage: (1) "are you a known app?" (service key), (2) "are you the right user?" (cookie + role).

Quick architecture note that justifies this: in Blazor Server, the page logic runs on the server and calls services *directly* (no HTTP). The API only matters for external callers — the downloader today, possibly other tools later — so gating *all* of it behind the key is clean and doesn't break the UI.

# Quebec's Cave — Full Final Plan (v7)

## 1. Stack

| Layer | Choice |
|---|---|
| Web + API | Blazor Server + Minimal API (one ASP.NET Core app, .NET 10) |
| Database | MS SQL Server (local default instance), accessed via `Microsoft.Data.SqlClient` |
| Schema versioning | DbUp running embedded `.sql` scripts on Web startup |
| User auth | Twitch OAuth (cookie session) |
| API auth | `X-Api-Key` header on every `/api/*` request; user/role checks layered on top |
| Console downloader | .NET 10 console wrapping `yt-dlp` |
| Test stack | MSTest + Moq + FluentAssertions + bUnit + WebApplicationFactory |
| Secrets — dev | `appsettings.Development.json` (gitignored) |
| Secrets — prod | `appsettings.json` placed on the prod box (committed file holds blanks) |
| Hosting | IIS on a 24/7 local box (you'll handle deploy) |
| Video delivery | Separate IIS site serving `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\...` at `https://vod.your-domain/...`. App stores URLs only. |

**Cross-cutting rules:**
- Async on every I/O method (DB, HTTP, file). Public methods accept `CancellationToken` where they can.
- Repository interfaces in `Core`, implementations in `Data`. Services depend on interfaces only.
- All admin mutations write to `AuditHistory`. Soft delete via `Deletion`.

## 2. Solution structure

```
Quebec's Cave.slnx
├── src/
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core         class lib — POCOs, interfaces, enums, validation. No I/O deps.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Data         class lib — Microsoft.Data.SqlClient repos, embedded SQL scripts, DbUp.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services     class lib — business logic, Twitch Helix client, file storage, time provider.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web          existing — Blazor pages + Minimal API endpoints.
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader   console — Twitch VOD watcher (yt-dlp wrapper).
├── tests/                       MSTest + Moq + FluentAssertions
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core.Tests
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services.Tests          (mocks IXxxRepository, ITwitchClient, IFileStorage)
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web.Tests               (+ bUnit, + WebApplicationFactory)
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader.Tests
└── docs/
    └── Database ERD.drawio
```

Dependency flow: `Web` & `Downloader` → `Services` → `Data` → `Core`. `Core` depends on nothing.

## 3. Branding & theme

**Cave Dark (default)**: bg `#1a1410` · surface `#2d2218` · accent `#d49a3a` · highlight `#e8c896` · text `#f4e9d8` · muted stone `#6b5d4f`.
**Forest Light**: bg `#f7efe1` · surface `#ffffff` · accent `#a06028` · text `#3d2818`.

- Theme applied via CSS variables on `<html data-theme="dark|light">`.
- Headings: chunky display font (Fredoka or Bricolage Grotesque). Body: Inter.
- Subtle stone-texture backgrounds on cards. Honey accent for hover/active. Mascot emojis (`quebCozy`, `quebDig`, `quebRaid`, etc.) used as section flair.
- Streamer's Twitch profile image used as the header logo (cached locally with the CDN URL as fallback).
- Sidebar: Streams · Games · Twitch link · login/profile · theme toggle.

## 4. Roles & permissions

| Role | Resolution | Capabilities |
|---|---|---|
| Anonymous | not logged in | Browse home, streams, games, watch videos |
| Viewer | logged in via Twitch | + react to videos |
| Moderator | Twitch user is in `ModeratorCache` (refreshed via Helix `/moderation/moderators`) | + access `/admin/reports` |
| Streamer | Twitch user ID = **`[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]`** | + full admin (games, streams, emojis, mod cache refresh, reports) |

Streamer logs in once with `moderation:read` and `user:read:broadcast` scopes; we hold his refresh token. A hosted service refreshes the mod cache every 15 min. If his token fails unrecoverably, a banner on `/admin` tells him to re-auth.

## 5. API auth model

Every `/api/*` endpoint goes through an authentication pipeline:

1. **Service key gate** (always required) — `X-Api-Key` header is matched (constant-time compare) against `Api:ServiceKeys` in config. No header / wrong key → `401`.
2. **User auth** (where required) — Twitch OAuth cookie session must exist. Missing / expired → `401`.
3. **Role check** (where required) — user's role (Streamer / Moderator / Viewer) must satisfy the endpoint's policy. Insufficient → `403`.

Implementation: a `RequireApiKey` authentication scheme + a `RequireUser` and `RequireRole(...)` policy chain, applied via endpoint filters or `[Authorize(Policy="...")]` on grouped routes. The Blazor pages call services directly and *never* hit the API over HTTP, so they bypass the key gate by construction. The downloader sends the key on every request.

## 6. Database (full schema)

ERD style mirrors the Hunter Industries reference: singular PascalCase, PK/FK rows, dedicated `AuditHistory` / `LoginAttempt` / `Deletion` lookup-style tables. Full diagram lives at `docs/Database ERD.drawio`.

```

  TwitchLogin     varchar(50)
  DisplayName     nvarchar(100)
  AvatarUrl       varchar(500)
  RoleId          FK → Role.RoleId
  ThemePreference varchar(10)  null         -- 'dark' | 'light' | null
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  LastSeenUtc     datetime2

  GameId          PK   int identity
  Name            nvarchar(150)

  TwitchVodId     varchar(50)   null
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  -- index on (StreamedUtc desc), (GameId)

Emoji

  UserId          FK → User.UserId
  EmojiId         FK → Emoji.EmojiId

  -- unique(StreamId, UserId, EmojiId)   ← Discord-style multi

StreamView
  StreamViewId    PK   int identity
  StreamId        FK → Stream.StreamId
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  IpHash          varbinary(32)              -- SHA-256
  ViewedUtc       datetime2

ModeratorCache
  ModeratorCacheId PK  int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  unique
  TwitchLogin     varchar(50)
  RefreshedUtc    datetime2

TwitchToken
  TwitchTokenId   PK   int identity
  UserId          FK → User.UserId
  AccessToken     varbinary(max)            -- DPAPI-encrypted
  RefreshToken    varbinary(max)            -- DPAPI-encrypted
  ExpiresUtc      datetime2
  Scopes          varchar(500)

LoginAttempt
  LoginAttemptId  PK   int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  null
  IpHash          varbinary(32)
  SucceededUtc    datetime2    null
  FailureReason   varchar(200) null
  AttemptedUtc    datetime2

AuditHistory
  AuditHistoryId  PK   int identity
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  Entity          varchar(50)
  EntityId        int
  Action          varchar(20)               -- Create | Update | Delete
  Diff            nvarchar(max)             -- json
  CreatedUtc      datetime2

Deletion
  DeletionId      PK   int identity
  Entity          varchar(50)
  EntityId        int
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  DeletedUtc      datetime2
```

## 7. Pages

**Public**
- `/` Home — hero with Twitch link, **live-now pill**, 6 newest stream cards.
- `/streams` — list with filters: game dropdown, date-range picker, free-text search, sort.
- `/games` — grid of game cards with icons → `/games/{slug}` (prefiltered streams).
- `/streams/{id}` — viewer: HTML5 `<video>` (or Twitch embed when `TwitchVodId` is set), Discord-style emoji reaction bar, related streams.
- `/login` — kicks off Twitch OAuth.

**Admin (streamer only unless flagged)**
- `/admin` — dashboard.
- `/admin/streams` — list + create/edit/delete; form has title, video URL (or upload to local storage), game, date, thumbnail, description.
- `/admin/games` — create/edit; "Fetch icon from Twitch" via Helix `/games?name=`, manual upload fallback.
- `/admin/emojis` — upload PNG, set code/name, toggle active, reorder.
- `/admin/reports` — **mods + streamer** — total views, total reactions, top streams, top games, reactions per emoji, growth over time, last-30-days chart.

## 8. API (every endpoint requires `X-Api-Key`)

**Public (key only)**
- `GET /api/streams?gameId=&from=&to=&q=&take=&skip=`
- `GET /api/streams/{id}`
- `GET /api/games`, `GET /api/games/{slug}`
- `GET /api/emojis`
- `GET /api/live-status`
- `POST /api/streams/{id}/view`

**Authenticated viewer (key + Twitch cookie)**
- `POST /api/streams/{id}/reactions { emojiId }` (idempotent)
- `DELETE /api/streams/{id}/reactions/{emojiId}`
- `GET /api/users/me`
- `GET/PUT /api/users/me/preferences { theme }`

**Mod or Streamer (key + cookie + role ∈ {Mod, Streamer})**
- `GET /api/admin/reports/*`

**Streamer only (key + cookie + role = Streamer)**
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/streams`
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/games`
- `POST/PUT/DELETE /api/admin/emojis`
- `POST /api/admin/upload-video` (multipart; saves under `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\{game-slug}\{year}\{vodId}.mp4`)
- `POST /api/admin/sync-mods`

**Service-only (key only, used by downloader)**
- `POST /api/ingest/streams`
- `GET /api/ingest/known-vod-ids`

## 9. Reactions (Discord-style)

- Multiple emojis per user per stream. Each emoji is independently toggleable.
- DB unique key: `(StreamId, UserId, EmojiId)`.
- API: `POST .../reactions {emojiId}` (idempotent), `DELETE .../reactions/{emojiId}`.
- UI: emoji bar on the viewer page; each chip shows count + lit/unlit state for current user.
- IP rate limit on POST/DELETE as defence-in-depth (e.g. 60 actions / 60s / IP).

## 10. Live-now pill

- `LiveStatusBackgroundService` polls Helix `GET /streams?user_id=[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]` every 60s using an app-credentials token.
- State exposed via singleton `ILiveStatusService` consumed by Blazor + the `/api/live-status` endpoint.
- Pill in the top bar; glowing honey accent + "LIVE" label + "Currently playing X" when live; hidden otherwise. Click → `https://twitch.tv/longlivequebec`.

## 11. Theme persistence

- On load:
  - If logged in → `GET /api/users/me/preferences`. If `theme` set, apply.
  - Else → read `localStorage["theme"]`. If set, apply.
  - Else → default Cave Dark.
- On toggle:
  - Always write `localStorage`.
  - If logged in → also `PUT /api/users/me/preferences { theme }`.
- On login → if API has no theme but `localStorage` does, push it up.

## 12. Dummy data (seeded if `Stream` is empty)

- All 28 emojis from `wwwroot/emojis/quebX.png`, populated into `Emoji` with `Code = quebX`.
- 4–5 sample games, icons fetched via Helix `/games?name=` at seed time.
- ~10 sample streams pointing at real `longlivequebec` Twitch VOD IDs (resolved via Helix `/videos?user_id=[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]&type=archive` at seed time). Viewer renders the Twitch embed for these.
- Sample reactions + views so `/admin/reports` has something to render.

## 13. Console downloader (`QuebecsCave.Downloader`)

- Reads `appsettings.json` (+ `appsettings.Development.json` overlay): API base URL, service API key, storage root, Twitch Client ID/Secret, broadcaster user ID `[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]`, poll interval seconds.
- Loop:
  1. App token (client credentials) → `GET /helix/videos?user_id=[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]&type=archive`.
  2. Diff against `GET /api/ingest/known-vod-ids` (sends `X-Api-Key`).
  3. For each new VOD: `yt-dlp -f best -o "{root}/{game-slug}/{year}/{vodId}.mp4" "https://twitch.tv/videos/{vodId}"`, also save thumbnail.
  4. `POST /api/ingest/streams` with metadata (sends `X-Api-Key`).
- Modes: `--once` (cron-friendly) or `--watch` (in-process loop).
- Logging via `Microsoft.Extensions.Logging` + Serilog console + rolling file.

# v8 Revisions — Audit History & Developer Role

## 4. Roles & permissions (revised)

| Role | Resolution | Capabilities |
|---|---|---|
| Anonymous | not logged in | Browse home, streams, games, watch videos |
| Viewer | logged in via Twitch | + react to videos |
| **Developer** | **Twitch user ID present in `Developer` table (managed by streamer)** | **+ access audit history pages** |
| Moderator | Twitch user is in `ModeratorCache` | + access `/admin/reports` + audit history pages |
| Streamer | Twitch user ID = `[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]` | + full admin (everything) |

Roles aren't strictly hierarchical anymore (a user might be only a Developer without being a Mod), so resolution becomes additive: a user has a *set* of capabilities derived from which lookups match. Streamer is still binary (you're him or you're not).

The streamer manages the developer list from `/admin/developers` (add by Twitch login → resolves to user ID via Helix → inserts row).

## 5. Database (additions)

Add `Role` seed values: `Streamer`, `Moderator`, `Viewer`, `Developer`.

The existing `AuditHistory` stays — it's specifically for **entity mutations** (admin-driven Create/Update/Delete with diff). The new audit pages use these new tables, mirroring the Hunter Industries `ErrorLog` pattern:

```
Developer
  DeveloperId      PK   int identity
  TwitchUserId     varchar(50)  unique
  TwitchLogin      varchar(50)
  AddedByUserId    FK → User.UserId
  AddedUtc         datetime2

ApiCallLog
  ApiCallLogId     PK   bigint identity
  Method           varchar(10)
  Path             varchar(500)
  QueryString      varchar(2000)  null
  RequestBody      nvarchar(max)  null     -- truncated to 4KB, sensitive fields redacted
  ResponseStatus   int
  ResponseBody     nvarchar(max)  null     -- truncated to 4KB
  UserId           FK → User.UserId  null
  IpHash           varbinary(32)
  ServiceKeyHash   varbinary(32)  null     -- which key was used (for downloader vs UI)
  DurationMs       int
  CalledUtc        datetime2
  RelatedAuditId   FK → AuditHistory.AuditHistoryId  null   -- links a POST/PUT/DELETE call to its entity-mutation record

DownloaderEvent
  DownloaderEventId PK  bigint identity
  Stage            varchar(30)             -- 'Poll' | 'TwitchAuth' | 'TwitchVodList' | 'Download' | 'Upload' | 'Ingest' | 'Heartbeat'
  TwitchVodId      varchar(50)   null
  Success          bit
  DurationMs       int           null
  Payload          nvarchar(max) null      -- json: request, response, command line, etc.
  Message          nvarchar(1000) null
  OccurredUtc      datetime2

WebsiteEvent
  WebsiteEventId   PK   bigint identity
  Action           varchar(50)             -- 'PageView' | 'Login' | 'Logout' | 'Reaction' | 'ThemeChange' | 'Search' etc.
  Path             varchar(500)  null
  UserId           FK → User.UserId  null
  IpHash           varbinary(32)
  Detail           nvarchar(max) null      -- json
  OccurredUtc      datetime2

ErrorStatus
  ErrorStatusId    PK   int identity
  Name             varchar(30)             -- seed: Open, Acknowledged, RaisedToGit, Fixed, NonIssue

ErrorLog
  ErrorLogId       PK   bigint identity
  Source           varchar(20)             -- 'Api' | 'Website' | 'Downloader' | 'BackgroundService'
  ExceptionType    varchar(200)
  Message          nvarchar(2000)
  StackTrace       nvarchar(max)
  Context          nvarchar(max) null      -- json: route, user, vodId, etc.
  StatusId         FK → ErrorStatus.ErrorStatusId      -- defaults to Open
  GitHubIssueUrl   varchar(500)  null
  AddressedByUserId FK → User.UserId  null
  AddressedUtc     datetime2     null
  Notes            nvarchar(max) null
  OccurredUtc      datetime2
  -- index on (OccurredUtc desc), (StatusId), (Source)
```

## 6. New & changed pages

**Sidebar — visible to Streamer / Mod / Developer:**
- New entry **"Audit History"** → `/admin/audit`. (Mods also still see "Reports". Streamer sees everything.)

**New pages**
- `/admin/audit` — landing page with four cards: **API Audit**, **Downloader Audit**, **Website Audit**, **Errors**. Each shows a count + the most recent entry.
- `/admin/audit/api` — paginated table. Columns: time · method · path · status · user · duration · IP. Filters: date range, user, endpoint contains, status code, method. Click a row → drawer with full request/response (redacted body), linked `AuditHistory` record if present.
- `/admin/audit/downloader` — paginated table. Columns: time · stage · VOD ID · success · duration · message. Filters: date range, stage, success/failure, VOD ID.
- `/admin/audit/website` — paginated table. Columns: time · action · user · path · IP. Filters: date range, user, action, path contains.
- `/admin/audit/errors` — paginated table. Columns: time · source · type · message · status · addressed by. Filters: date range, source, status, exception type, free-text. Row drawer shows full stack + context + workflow buttons:
  - **Acknowledge** → status = Acknowledged
  - **Raise to GitHub** → opens a modal for issue URL, status = RaisedToGit
  - **Mark fixed** → status = Fixed
  - **Mark non-issue** → status = NonIssue
  - Free-text **notes** field
- `/admin/developers` — **streamer only** — manage the developer allowlist (add by Twitch login, remove).

## 8. API additions (all behind `X-Api-Key` as before)

**Audit-access endpoints (key + cookie + role ∈ {Streamer, Mod, Developer})**
- `GET /api/admin/audit/api?...` (paginated, filters as above)
- `GET /api/admin/audit/downloader?...`
- `GET /api/admin/audit/website?...`
- `GET /api/admin/audit/errors?...`
- `GET /api/admin/audit/errors/{id}` (detail)
- `PUT /api/admin/audit/errors/{id}/status { statusId, gitHubIssueUrl?, notes? }`

**Streamer-only**
- `GET/POST/DELETE /api/admin/developers`

**Service-only (downloader)**
- `POST /api/ingest/downloader-events` (batched array)
- `POST /api/ingest/errors` (batched array)

## Implementation notes

**API call logging** — middleware on the `/api/*` group:
- Wraps the request, captures method/path/query, body (cap 4KB), status, duration, user, IP, and which service key was used (hash, not value).
- **Redaction**: a small allowlist-driven sanitizer removes/masks fields named `clientSecret`, `accessToken`, `refreshToken`, `apiKey`, `password`, `authorization` (any case) before persisting.
- **Async write**: events queued via a `Channel<T>` and flushed by a `BackgroundService` in batches of N or every M ms — never blocks the request path.
- **Volume guard**: `Audit:ApiCallLog:Enabled` (default true) and `Audit:ApiCallLog:SamplingRate` config so it's easy to dial down later.

**Website event logging** — a thin `IWebsiteEventLogger` service called from Blazor pages on key actions (login, page view, reaction, theme change, search). Same async-batch pipeline as API logging.

**Downloader event logging** — every stage of the loop wraps in `using var _ = await _events.Track(stage, vodId)` which captures duration + outcome and posts to `/api/ingest/downloader-events`. Buffers locally if API is unreachable, retries on next loop.

**Error capture**:
- Web: a global `IExceptionHandler` (ASP.NET Core 10's built-in interface) writes to `ErrorLog` with route + user + correlation ID, then re-throws. Background services wrap their work the same way.
- Downloader: try/catch around the loop body, posts to `/api/ingest/errors`. Logs locally too in case the API itself is down.

**Linking** — when an admin mutation happens, the entity-mutation `AuditHistory` row's ID is written into the corresponding `ApiCallLog.RelatedAuditId` so the audit detail drawer can show "this call modified Stream #42 — view diff".

**Retention** — for v1, no automatic retention; we keep everything. Worth revisiting if `ApiCallLog` grows past a few GB. A nightly job is trivial to add later if needed.

## Phasing (insertions)

Existing phases shift; the audit work lands as:

- **3.5 Audit infrastructure (new)** — schema additions (Developer, ApiCallLog, DownloaderEvent, WebsiteEvent, ErrorStatus, ErrorLog), API call logging middleware + async-batch writer, global exception handler → ErrorLog, ingest endpoints for downloader-events and errors. No UI yet.
- **7. Admin pages** (existing) — extends to cover `/admin/audit/*` pages, error workflow actions, and `/admin/developers`. Sidebar shows "Audit History" for Streamer/Mod/Developer.
- **9. Console downloader** (existing) — wraps every stage in event tracking and posts `DownloaderEvent`s and `ErrorLog`s to the API.

Everything else from v7 stands.

---

Open question that affects scope:

- For `ApiCallLog`, do you want the **request and response bodies** captured by default, or just the metadata (method/path/status/duration/user)? Bodies are very useful for debugging but bulk up storage and risk leaking sensitive data even with redaction. I'd default to **metadata only**, with a config flag `Audit:ApiCallLog:CaptureBodies` (default `true` in dev, `false` in prod) — but tell me if you want them on always.

# Quebec's Cave — Full Final Plan (v9)

## 1. Stack

| Layer | Choice |
|---|---|
| Web + API | Blazor Server + Minimal API (one ASP.NET Core app, .NET 10) |
| Database | MS SQL Server (local default instance), accessed via `Microsoft.Data.SqlClient` |
| Schema versioning | DbUp running embedded `.sql` scripts on Web startup |
| User auth | Twitch OAuth (cookie session) |
| API auth | `X-Api-Key` header on every `/api/*` request; user/role checks layered on top |
| Console downloader | .NET 10 console wrapping `yt-dlp` |
| Test stack | MSTest + Moq + FluentAssertions + bUnit + WebApplicationFactory |
| Secrets — dev | `appsettings.Development.json` (gitignored) |
| Secrets — prod | `appsettings.json` placed on the prod box (committed file holds blanks) |
| Hosting | IIS on a 24/7 local box (you'll handle deploy) |
| Video delivery | Separate IIS site serving `D:\QuebecsCave\videos\...` at `https://vod.your-domain/...`. App stores URLs only. |

**Cross-cutting rules:**
- Async on every I/O method (DB, HTTP, file). Public methods accept `CancellationToken` where they can.
- Repository interfaces in `Core`, implementations in `Data`. Services depend on interfaces only.
- All admin entity mutations write to `AuditHistory`. Soft delete via `Deletion`.
- Every `/api/*` HTTP call writes to `ApiCallLog` (metadata only by default).

## 2. Solution structure

```
Quebec's Cave.slnx
├── src/
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core         class lib — POCOs, interfaces, enums, validation. No I/O deps.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Data         class lib — Microsoft.Data.SqlClient repos, embedded SQL scripts, DbUp.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services     class lib — business logic, Twitch Helix client, file storage, audit.
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web          existing — Blazor pages + Minimal API endpoints.
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader   console — Twitch VOD watcher (yt-dlp wrapper).
├── tests/                       MSTest + Moq + FluentAssertions
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Core.Tests
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Services.Tests
│   ├── QuebecsCave.Web.Tests               (+ bUnit, + WebApplicationFactory)
│   └── QuebecsCave.Downloader.Tests
└── docs/
    └── Database ERD.drawio
```

Dependency flow: `Web` & `Downloader` → `Services` → `Data` → `Core`. `Core` depends on nothing.

## 3. Branding & theme

**Cave Dark (default)**: bg `#1a1410` · surface `#2d2218` · accent `#d49a3a` · highlight `#e8c896` · text `#f4e9d8` · muted stone `#6b5d4f`.
**Forest Light**: bg `#f7efe1` · surface `#ffffff` · accent `#a06028` · text `#3d2818`.

- Theme applied via CSS variables on `<html data-theme="dark|light">`.
- Headings: chunky display font (Fredoka or Bricolage Grotesque). Body: Inter.
- Subtle stone-texture backgrounds on cards. Honey accent for hover/active. Mascot emojis (`quebCozy`, `quebDig`, `quebRaid`, etc.) used as section flair.
- Streamer's Twitch profile image as the header logo (cached locally, CDN URL fallback).
- Sidebar: Streams · Games · (audit + reports + admin entries depending on role) · Twitch link · login/profile · theme toggle.

## 4. Roles & permissions

Roles are **additive sets**, not strictly hierarchical. A user can be (e.g.) just a Developer.

| Role | Resolution | Capabilities |
|---|---|---|
| Anonymous | not logged in | Browse home, streams, games, watch videos |
| Viewer | logged in via Twitch | + react to videos |
| Developer | Twitch user ID present in `Developer` table (managed by streamer) | + access audit history pages |
| Moderator | Twitch user is in `ModeratorCache` (refreshed via Helix `/moderation/moderators`) | + access reports + audit history pages |
| Streamer | Twitch user ID = **`[REDACTED-TWITCH-ID]`** | + full admin (everything) |

The streamer manages the developer list at `/admin/developers` (add by Twitch login → resolves to user ID via Helix → inserts row).

The streamer logs in once with `moderation:read` and `user:read:broadcast` scopes; we hold his refresh token. A hosted service refreshes the mod cache every 15 min. If his token fails unrecoverably, a banner on `/admin` tells him to re-auth.

## 5. API auth model

Every `/api/*` endpoint passes through:

1. **Service key gate** — `X-Api-Key` matched (constant-time) against `Api:ServiceKeys`. Missing/wrong → `401`.
2. **User auth** (where required) — Twitch OAuth cookie session. Missing/expired → `401`.
3. **Role check** (where required) — user's role-set must include the required role(s). Insufficient → `403`.

Blazor pages call services directly (no HTTP), so the key gate never affects the UI.

## 6. Database (full schema)

ERD style mirrors the Hunter Industries reference: singular PascalCase, PK/FK rows, dedicated `AuditHistory` / `LoginAttempt` / `ErrorLog` / `Deletion` lookup-style tables. Full diagram lives at `docs/Database ERD.drawio`.

```
Role
  RoleId          PK   int identity
  Name            varchar(20)              -- Streamer | Moderator | Viewer | Developer

User
  UserId          PK   int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  unique
  TwitchLogin     varchar(50)
  DisplayName     nvarchar(100)
  AvatarUrl       varchar(500)
  ThemePreference varchar(10)  null         -- 'dark' | 'light' | null
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  LastSeenUtc     datetime2

Developer
  DeveloperId     PK   int identity
  TwitchUserId    varchar(50)  unique
  TwitchLogin     varchar(50)
  AddedByUserId   FK → User.UserId
  AddedUtc        datetime2

Game
  GameId          PK   int identity
  Name            nvarchar(150)
  Slug            varchar(150)  unique
  IconUrl         varchar(500)
  TwitchGameId    varchar(50)   null
  IsCustomIcon    bit
  CreatedUtc      datetime2

Stream
  StreamId        PK   int identity
  Title           nvarchar(300)
  Description     nvarchar(max) null
  GameId          FK → Game.GameId
  StreamedUtc     datetime2
  DurationSeconds int
  VideoUrl        varchar(500)
  ThumbnailUrl    varchar(500)
  TwitchVodId     varchar(50)   null
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  -- index on (StreamedUtc desc), (GameId)

Emoji
  EmojiId         PK   int identity
  Code            varchar(50)   unique     -- e.g. 'quebKing'
  Name            varchar(100)
  ImageUrl        varchar(500)
  IsActive        bit
  SortOrder       int

Reaction
  ReactionId      PK   int identity
  StreamId        FK → Stream.StreamId
  UserId          FK → User.UserId
  EmojiId         FK → Emoji.EmojiId
  CreatedUtc      datetime2
  -- unique(StreamId, UserId, EmojiId)   ← Discord-style multi

StreamView
  StreamViewId    PK   int identity
  StreamId        FK → Stream.StreamId
  UserId          FK → User.UserId  null
  IpHash          varbinary(32)              -- SHA-256
  ViewedUtc       datetime2
```
